  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f1c078f9-7c0e-4968-b8d9-046e54fdf523'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText10931830924804296171" style="display:none"><b>Magnus Bane has a royal role in the French Revolution—if the angry mobs don’t spoil his spells. One of ten adventures in The Bane Chronicles.</b><br /><br />While in France, immortal warlock Magnus Bane finds himself attempting to rescue the royal family from the horrors of the French Revolution—after being roped into this mess by a most attractive count. Naturally, the daring escape calls for invisible air balloons…<br /><br />This standalone e-only short story illuminates the life of the enigmatic Magnus Bane, whose alluring personality populates the pages of the #1 <i>New York Times </i>bestselling series, The Mortal Instruments and The Infernal Devices series. This story in The Bane Chronicles, <i>The Runaway Queen</i>, is written by Maureen Johnson and Cassandra Clare.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>  </div>

<div id="review_595492270" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595492270" />
    <a title="Gerasimos Reads " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11731184-gerasimos-reads"><img alt="Gerasimos Reads " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601542847p2/11731184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/595492270?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerasimos Reads " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerasimos Reads " href="/user/show/11731184-gerasimos-reads">Gerasimos Reads </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595492270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7530748165164824162">I love Cassandra Clare! Her world and characters earned a place in my heart. <br/><br/>The first story in this short-story series <i>What Really Happened in Peru</i> was very enjoyable and fun but nothing too special. I enjoyed it but I wanted to see more.<br/><br/>My main problem with the first story was that it was actually four short stories set around Peru. But this second story was one story with a beginning, a middle and an end. <br/><br/>It was hilarious, enjoyable and fun! While I was reading it I forgot about my problems a</span>
  <span id="freeText7530748165164824162" style="display:none">I love Cassandra Clare! Her world and characters earned a place in my heart. <br /><br />The first story in this short-story series <i>What Really Happened in Peru</i> was very enjoyable and fun but nothing too special. I enjoyed it but I wanted to see more.<br /><br />My main problem with the first story was that it was actually four short stories set around Peru. But this second story was one story with a beginning, a middle and an end. <br /><br />It was hilarious, enjoyable and fun! While I was reading it I forgot about my problems and the real world and I got lost into Paris, Versailles and the French Revolution. Hanging out with the crazy Magnus Bane, Marie Antoinette and Axel Von Fersen was so much fun! I always travel into Clare's world! The setting of this story was so much more interesting than in the first one!<br /><br />And again Cassandra Clare managed to put a few sweet heartwarming moments into the crazy adventures of Magnus and his friends that is also something I love about her!<br /><br />Getting to know more about Magnus Bane was something I always wanted! You can never get enough of Magnus! If you loved the first story you will be amazed but this second one. And if you don't, I believe that you will love this! <br /><br />I don't really get why people say that Clare is overdoing it with the Shadowhunters world! Since her stories are so different and the only similarity in them is that they're set in the same world, I don't really get it. It is like saying that you are bored of stories set in the real world, in our world. Not all Realistic Fiction stories are the same! This is the case with Clare's book for me as well! And as long as they continue to be so good I will keep reading them!<br /><br />I cannot really wait for the third short story in the Bane Chronicles! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7530748165164824162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  </b>
</blockquote><br />This short story follows Magnus in Paris during the French Revolution in 1791. And apparently Paris is the place to be if you’re a vampire (which I highkey love, actually). Magnus attends a party with Henri de Polignac, then meets Axel von Fersen and accepts a difficult mission to smuggle Marie Antoinette and her family out of the city, before the desperate people take matters into their own hands. Of course, nothing goes as planned, and Magnus somehow acquires a pet monkey that he names Ragnor, but it was still a really enjoyable story and adventure. <br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br /><br />(I read this in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2552335362" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bane Chronicles</a>!) ✨</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17093686526437159349"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Boring. Though I do have to say that it wasn't quite as dire as <i>What Really Happened in Peru</i>, which was just a mish-mash of random scenes in Peru. At least <i>The Runaway Queen</i> had some sort of a cohesive plot. <br/><br/>Unfortunately, the story was dull and unimaginative… Magnus is in Paris, and wants to ride a hot air balloon, the weather's rubbish so he can't. Some guy called Axel wants Magnus to help him save Marie Antoinette… Because Magnus is randy and easily falls for good looking guys, he say</span>
  <span id="freeText17093686526437159349" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Boring. Though I do have to say that it wasn't quite as dire as <i>What Really Happened in Peru</i>, which was just a mish-mash of random scenes in Peru. At least <i>The Runaway Queen</i> had some sort of a cohesive plot. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the story was dull and unimaginative… Magnus is in Paris, and wants to ride a hot air balloon, the weather's rubbish so he can't. Some guy called Axel wants Magnus to help him save Marie Antoinette… Because Magnus is randy and easily falls for good looking guys, he says yes to Axel in the hopes that he'll drop his knickers for him. Also, some french vampires act cheesy and cliched, and Magnus is wary of them because they're really scary or some shit. Then he finally gets to ride in his hot air balloon in a <s>daring</s> boring escape. The end. <br />Oh and Magnus somehow gets a monkey. I was more interested in how Magnus ended up with said monkey than I was with his troubles with the French vampires and royalty. Sadly, his monkey adoption adventure of sorts was glossed over.<br /><br />Magnus had very little personality, his voice was supremely dull, his adventures should have been somewhat exciting but his POV made everything sound so blah. <br /><br />I'm beginning to think that Magnus only wants Alec for his looks — he's obsessed with blue eyed, black haired guys. I think if Alec was blond and brown eyed, Magnus wouldn't be all that attracted to him. <br /><br />I really do hate Magnus, I used to like him… But his angsty-boring-teenage-emo personality annoys me. And I hate how he gets lusty and passionate about every person he meets — but he's never acted so hot and bothered around Alec, yet he's meant to be in love with him. Ugh.<br />My one wish for <i>The Mortal Instruments</i> series is that Alec falls out of love with Magnus, and then dates around, and eventually meets and falls for some sexy shadowhunter guy. That'll show <i>the-I-fall for-everyone-I-meet-slut</i> Magnus.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_622515558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622515558" />
    <a title="Andre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6431131-andre"><img alt="Andre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378118123p2/6431131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622515558?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre" href="/user/show/6431131-andre">Andre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=not-really-worth-reading">not-really-worth-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6431131-andre?shelf=bisexual">bisexual</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622515558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer390019278271762884">A friend of mine wrote: <i>shit like this usually happens in some badly written fanfics. Plus all self-respecting fanfic writers won't make such a mistake anyway.</i><br/><br/>As easy as it is to show what is wrong with this book, as easy would it be to do better for everybody reading this book with just a little effort and an honest editor. But apparently these authors had neither.<br/>How can you do so much wrong in so little time? And I personally think this book was only better (not good!) than the 1st not becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText390019278271762884" style="display:none">A friend of mine wrote: <i>shit like this usually happens in some badly written fanfics. Plus all self-respecting fanfic writers won't make such a mistake anyway.</i><br /><br />As easy as it is to show what is wrong with this book, as easy would it be to do better for everybody reading this book with just a little effort and an honest editor. But apparently these authors had neither.<br />How can you do so much wrong in so little time? And I personally think this book was only better (not good!) than the 1st not because of the writers but rather because it was shorter and only dealt with one story; fewer chances to mess up, but they used them to full advantage. <br /><br />If you follow these five steps you may enjoy this book:<br />1. Completely eradicate any sort of disbelief.<br />2. Throw logic out of the window<br />3. Have no knowledge of normal human behavior.<br />4. Do not know any other of Clare's books and if you do erase their content from your memory.<br />5. Do not know history.<br /><br />Even if you say that the historical events are correctly referred to (which they are clearly not or at least it is very weird to just gloss them over) there is still the problem of their cliché usage and the characters, first among them Magnus himself. Instead of the backstabbing arrogant asshole of the first book, here he was a fashion-obsessed, cock-crazy diva who cared about nothing but himself and was so dumb that Bella Swan from the Twilight looks like a genius next to him. Well either that or he cares so little for other people even when they are part of a job that he cannot think of the most efficient ways to use his magic. In that case he is just plain selfish.<br /><br />And the story itself was not only cliché it was all so jumbled together that it was hard to say whether something was historically inaccurate or one of the many plotholes. And there were many, so incredibly many, the whole book had so many clichés, inaccuracies and plotholes it was unbelievable. <br />And before anybody says "it's just fiction", think of this:<br />On average when you insert actual historical events into your story people will automatically consider this to be the grain of truth, that is a fact. So as an author you have the responsibility to make sure that what you use is as accurate as possible to the best of your abilities and I think this is not what the author's did. If it were, it would not have been so easy for me to spot all the errors. <br /><br />The start was already so horrible and my trust in the authors' writing abilities was so low I found myself asking questions about nearly every second sentence and that only after the first 4 pages. And these pages were small, quite small.<br />And I just don't understand what they are doing. They already messed up the character in "What happened in Peru" and it is no better here. And why are they doing this? This is not fair to the fans whom they make hate this version of Magnus. I never really liked Magnus because of his major character flaws but I readily admit that he wasn't this asshole in Clare's other series. As bad as he was he came not even close to this.<br /><br />Ok, I said my opinion about this book without spoiling anything, so here is the spoiler section which for convenience I structured into several points. This is not all there was, just the most obvious:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br /><b>1) This is history?</b><br /><br />Magnus's statement that Marie Antoinette, when told that her people could not afford bread, had <i>suggested that they eat cake instead.</i> is not only a cliché but wrong. Apart from the fact that its "brioche" (a special sort of breed) and not cake, there is no record that this was ever said by Antoinette or any opponent of the monarchy. It was first attributed to her by Alphonse Karr more than 50 years later, probably because of the fact that even during her lifetime she had problems in France because of her gender and Austrian birth, by the time this statement came to be she was only a child and not even in France.<br /><br />The book states that there were periodic killings, fires and attacks, but references nothing to point towards any historical events. I did my best to look it up and found nothing that fits. <br /><br />The book mentions some sort of vampire craze in 1787 and missing children at the time. Whether there were missing children during that year; I could find nothing, and on the supposed nephew and niece of the Duke de Polignac that appear here, also nothing. <br /><br />The book glosses over the Women's March on Versailles with the sentence <i>The peasant women had broken into the palace of Versailles</i>. You would think someone living in Paris for 6 years would at least know some numbers (it was a mob of thousands and neither entirely female), and they neither broke in nor was it as harmless as Magnus makes it out to be. The same with other events, it is just weird that he glosses this stuff over so much, especially since Magnus claims that it was important that people should have all basics of life. Basically Magnus does not come along as a character who lived through all this.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>2) They expect us to believe that?</b><br /><br />Supposedly <i>In Paris one could have the eyes of a cat (as he did) and tell people it was a trick of fashion.</i> All these people belief it is a fashion trick? How is that possible back then? And no one wants to know how that works? And the book clearly stated that his eyes were visible.<br />And that is not even the basic problem: According to Clare Magnus is "Asian", whatever that means. Marie Antoinette was as pale as can be and she already had problems due to being born in Austria, Magnus was born in Jakarta and he is just accepted into high society? And why does no history book mention him (not even inside the Clareverse)?<br /><br />Apparently Magnus can find a lot of work because the aristocracy of Paris is into magic. And not just card or table tricks, nope its speaking monkeys, birds singing operas, fire fountains etc. <br /><br />Magnus speaks the Swedish sentence <i>"If you wrap me in furs, I can pretend to be your little fuzzy bear."</i> Who in the late 18th century would talk like that? <br /><br />That Axel von Fersen seriously believes that people will not recognize their king because the king is not handsome and they only take note of his clothes and carriage. Surprise, the book itself states that the flight doesn't work because someone recognized the king, not the queen as he claimed (no idea whether she was still glamoured at the time or not), but the king. Which is actually what you would expect in that day and age. The monarchy had so many enemies of course they would the face of the king and queen.<br /><br />Marie Antoinette stays totally calm when she hears Magnus's voice in her bed chambers coming out of nowhere and just resumes her pacing. This woman has been under surveilance for about 2 years and nearly got killed once and she just stays calm? She doesn't get suspicious?<br /><br />When she gets captured by the vampires of Paris (where she acts like a blabbering idiot instead of the queen) these idiots (especially the supposedly badass head vampire) believe Magnus's stupid story about her being a job by a costumer, who paid to have some women act and look like the queen. <br /><br />And by the way that big bad head vampire apparently has the nephew and niece of the Duke de Polignac as his underlings. Now the Duke's wife is a close confident of Marie Antoinette and that big bad vampire does not try to profit from it?<br /><br />Magnus can reach with his mind all over Paris, take possession of a rolled up balloon, roll it, make it inflate itself, glamour it invisible and guide it with his mind towards him, avoiding several buildings in the process, but he does not have his energey to get himself and the queen out by any other method. What happened with making carpets fly as the start of the book stated? <br /><br />This is not simply hard to believe it is one giant plothole and to be honest all examples of point 1 and 2 could easily fit into the now coming point 3.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>3) Plotholes over plotholes </b><br /><br />Magnus was in Paris in 1791, the same year he was, according to the 1st book, in Peru. The 2nd book refers to the Flight to Varennes, so it was around the 21thJune1791 and afterwards he was in the Alps for several weeks. So he could not have left Europe before July. When was he in Peru? How did he get there so fast? Even the fastest ship would need weeks. Was it a portal or what? <br /><br />Magnus has a cabriolet carriage and the author writes that it was <i>brutally hot inside</i>, but how can that be if it is open at the front? And would he even need a fan in that case, would it be of any use? <br />And speaking of that little fan:<br />Magnus animated it for cooling… A cabriolet is open at the front, where is the fan placed to be hidden? Also Magnus can only make a fan that can <i>barely stir a breeze</i>? In the last book he was stated to have caused earthquakes.<br /><br />As part of the magic he performs for the high society Magnus mentions stars appearing on cheeks, heart shaped beauty-spots, flame shooting fountains and even speaking monkeys, birds singing operas, diamonds glowing in different colors and chaise longues wandering across the room. If people think his magic is real why don't they demand more serious stuff?<br /><br />He covers for rain in the cabriolet although just minutes ago he cast a spell to make it that the rain <i>rolled off an invisible canopy</i> over his head. Did it suddenly wear off or what?<br /><br /><i>Axel was worth</i> all the trouble this job brought Magnus. He barely knows the guy and the ending of the book doesn't suggest that <i>Axel was worth it.</i> And why does Axel trust Magnus so much?<br /><br />Magnus only makesa spark in a corner to distract a guard in front of the queen's chamber but when entering the building he used a glamour that made him appear like a large cat. Why not make the guy fall asleep?<br /><br />How did the Queen get lost in the city if she was supposed to be with the Marquise? And if Magnus knows that Paris is full of vampires and it is blackest night, why did he not cast a glamour that also works on vampires? <br /><br />Why can the head vampire Marcel Saint Cloud just raise a hand and silence the queen? Did he enchante her? Does he have such presence?<br /><br />Although the queen had remained calm when guns where pointed at her in the past here she faints when entering the invisible balloon and later on she is mostly unconscious and when they crash land into the Seine she is suddenly unconscious again. I personally think this is simply so they don't have to write the queen as an actual character, because she is not. She is a queen of Marie Antoinette. As flawed a character as she might have been, she was no damsel in distress like in this book. And no it doesn not count that she is suddenly in the supernatural world because strength of character and strong nerves don't just dissapear like that.<br />And when they are out of the Seine we learn that it was agreed that <i>Magnus was to send a blue flash into the sky</i> should anything go wrong. Then why did he leave right after he glamoured the queen? Did he not tell Axel that he wouldn't be there all the time?<br />And when all was done suddenly and in front of everybody Axel kissed Magnus despite there never being any hint of attraction. Not to mention the time and place.<br /><br />Later Magnus is visited by the head vampire underling Henri who tells him, should he decline the invitation, Paris would be a very uncomfortable place for Magnus. Then Magnus says that he didn't want to offense anyone and that he accepts his <i>punishment.</i> What punishment? There is no mentioning of any punishment, and considered that after he gets his stuff the next we read is about him somewhere in the Alps there is no mentioning of any punishment whatsoever.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>4) Can you really do nothing else but cliché?</b><br /><br />A litte list of clichés in the books:<br />1) French aristocracy has special needs in terms of sex<br />2) French society was the most decadent Magnus had ever met<br />3) The worst thing about Henri is that he is boring in Magnus's eyes.<br />4) Henri calls his vampire master just "Master"? Basically he sounds like cliché Igor.<br />5) Bothering Magnus is of course sooo bad. <br />6) There was an attractive man with black hair and blue eyes, who wears expensive clothes of <i>obviously fine quality</i> and whom Magnus has the hots for, you know just like any other Clare book where he appears, the guy is either there in person or part of Magnus's type.<br />7) Marie Antoinette and Hans Axel Graf (Count) von Fersen appear in this novel and interact with Magnus and at least Axel has the hots for the queen. Never mind that an actual affair between Fersen and the Queen is impossible to verify and probably unlikely since she was rarely ever alone for long.<br />8) Saint Cloud possible knew the vampire Vlad Tepez and is a very attractive vampire.<br />9) The Marquis de Sade was at the vampire party.<br />10) The queen wanders off, gets lost and captured by the vampires.<br /><br />These are really not all there were, believe me I wish there were.<br /><br /><br /><b>5) Magnus always Magnus </b><br /><br />Magnus still mostly cares about his fashion (he needs 1-2 hours to dress for opera, and considered that he can do magic does that mean he cannot decide what to wear? Shouldn't he know after more than 100 years of living?) and downright states that he has to or go naked. What he likes about Paris and what he mostly notices are material things and appearances (even wasting precious time), except of course when its Axel there its also some personality traits.<br />And I really wonder what Magnus considers to be friendship. Because his friends apparently allow him a lot and now its <i>problematic</i> to be seen in their company. What friend talks that way and what does he do for them?<br /><br /><i>It really was getting difficult to be wonderful.</i><br />This is what Magnus thinks when he walks through the Bois de Boulogne where people grow potatoes for food. Supposedly he <i>always felt for the poor and the wretched.</i> In the whole book he never does anything out of altruism, not even a hint. He could have let said potatoes grow bigger but he does nothing. He doesn't even seem to feel enough for them to endure the smell, nope Magnus rather smells at a jasmine-scented cloth. He seems to be annoyed by everything and his behavior reflects none of the many dangers and troubles he supposedly faces. And the authors literally state that there was <i>nothing Magnus attached more importance to than a whim.</i> And apparently that really fits because he considers leaving Paris for some other locations because of the problematic situation with the revolution and suddenly he says <i>Perhaps it was best to stay in Paris.</i> No explanation whatsoever. And not only his he cock-crazy for Von Fersen Magnus apparently cannot even remember the name of one of his more recent “lovers” despite spending the night at her place. How many "lovers" does he have on average? And by the way if you do not remember the name its not a "lover" its a hook-up.<br /><br />The authors waste no possibility to shove it into our face how much Magnus has the hots for Axel. Well apparently not enough to make him write to Axel and make him stop going to Paris or to go to him and help him although the two separated on good terms and there was nothing mentioned about any problems. He actually refuses to help because he cannot deal with "mundane politics?" Asshole, plain and simple, asshole. I wish in her next book in TMI Clare would kill him but sadly I don't think so. Based on her Bane Chronicles so far I am pretty sure she will let him be with Alec again. And now I tell you why I think that.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>6) Why don't you just say so outright? </b><br /><br />The authors constantly point out in all those non-TMI books that Magnus's favorite traits are black hair and blue eyes and throw references in (here it was the sudden kiss). We get it; Alec is supposed to be perfect for him. Von Fersen's look fits right in, because you know there is no real consistency on how Von Fersen looked. The descriptions vary regarding eyes and hair. And there was also this little typo where they typed “Alex” instead of “Axel”. Which made me wonder whether she chose to use the name "Axel" because of its similarity to "Alec." After all what two strangers from that time and that society level instantly adress each other with first name even if they have the hots for each other?<br /><br />And why do the authors even bother with it? Just get some fortune teller who tells Magnus that his "big love" will have these traits; maybe even give some details so he can recognize him. At least that would be an explanation for his mercurial dating/relationship habits.<br />Also it would save time and space that could be used for actual important information.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This is only a severely shortened version of this spoiler section and review but I think it should be sufficient. If you are interested in the full review you would have to visit my deviantart journal: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fav.me/d66nljk">http://fav.me/d66nljk</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="390019278271762884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review592713141">
  <td colspan="2">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer625490275" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18086660100418015753">The low rating is for my own personal shelving purposes and does not reflect on the writing or story itself.<br/><br/>I am reading these just to make sure I don't miss any clues or hints about the bigger picture in general, but am not a big fan of most "side stories" for series, with a few rare exceptions. I'd rather just read it all in the main books, so I am kind of halfheartedly skimming these just to make sure I don't miss anything because it's not unlike Clare to slip little details in that connect t</span>
  <span id="freeText18086660100418015753" style="display:none">The low rating is for my own personal shelving purposes and does not reflect on the writing or story itself.<br><br>I am reading these just to make sure I don't miss any clues or hints about the bigger picture in general, but am not a big fan of most "side stories" for series, with a few rare exceptions. I'd rather just read it all in the main books, so I am kind of halfheartedly skimming these just to make sure I don't miss anything because it's not unlike Clare to slip little details in that connect to the bigger picture.<br><br>That's all. No real complaints here. Ignore the rating.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380423057i/842566.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_622060965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622060965" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622060965?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622060965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5702817216639652554">So, this review is titled 'Cassandra Clare makes bad decisions (and I'm not talking about that <u>Mortal Instruments</u> anthology)' *shudders* - because compared to <u>What Really Happened in Peru</u> (nothing), <u>The Runaway Queen</u> is actually... decent. Or at least we still have all the usual problems inherent with writing a ten part short story collection, the elaborate fan fiction aspect, the less than hundred pages not being nearly enough for any character or plot development of note problem, the obvious m</span>
  <span id="freeText5702817216639652554" style="display:none">So, this review is titled 'Cassandra Clare makes bad decisions (and I'm not talking about that <u>Mortal Instruments</u> anthology)' *shudders* - because compared to <u>What Really Happened in Peru</u> (nothing), <u>The Runaway Queen</u> is actually... decent. Or at least we still have all the usual problems inherent with writing a ten part short story collection, the elaborate fan fiction aspect, the less than hundred pages not being nearly enough for any character or plot development of note problem, the obvious money grab angle, but at least Maureen Johnson seems to be actually trying here (for the most part). I love Sarah Rees Brennan (or her writing style and <u>Unspoken</u> at least), but <u>What Really Happened in Peru</u> was so obviously pointless filler and Brennan's style just too flashy for historical, Johnson I think has a much better hand for the material and while the plot's definitely still filler, at least there is a plot to speak of. That actually matches real history. <br /><br />Which brings me back to why I titled the review the way I did:<br /><br /><b>Bad decision number one - skimping out on an editor</b>: This one isn't even funny. There are obvious typos like a character being named Axel <i>and</i> Alex and random names left as blanks, at this point I doubt anyone still thinks Clare cares but come on at least keep up the illusion.<br /><br /><b>Bad decision number two - letting Johnson write Magnus off a cheat sheet</b>: His character is so by the books I should be laughing - from being insulted. There's his flashy dress. The usual gay references. A monkey. And that's it. Brennan's take may have been outrageously anachronistic, but Johnson's is just flat. There's something seriously wrong when the setting's well written and the character is... not. <br /><br /><b>Bad decision number three - not making this the first short story</b>: With the obvious difference in quality, you gotta hook 'em in before you slack off. Despite flat Magnus my overall impression is way more favorable with this one and I definitely think anyone who's read both will see why this should've been first. And she's supposed to be a marketing genius. Lol.<br /><br />Tldr(really?): I doubt Cassandra Clare even read these before hawking them to the general public.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5702817216639652554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_708240612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/708240612" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/708240612?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer708240612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12558982165406807192">This story takes place in Paris in 1791. Magnus has been enjoying his time there but is approached by someone asking Magnus to help the King and Queen escape imprisonment so that they might be restored to the throne. Also, there is contact between Magnus and Marcel Saint Cloud, the head of the Paris Vampire Clan. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1376195731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1376195731" />
    <a title="Thibaut Nicodème" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22674620-thibaut-nicod-me"><img alt="Thibaut Nicodème" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574079623p2/22674620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1376195731?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thibaut Nicodème" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thibaut Nicodème" href="/user/show/22674620-thibaut-nicod-me">Thibaut Nicodème</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22674620-thibaut-nicod-me?shelf=snark">snark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1376195731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5033117671413652443">Full review <a href='http://snarktheater.tumblr.com/post/133949388634/the-bane-chronicles-the-runaway-queen' rel='nofollow noopener'>on my blog, the Snark Theater</a>.<br/><br/>In this story, Magnus helps Queen Marie Antoinette escape the Tuileries, as well as a bunch of vampires. If you know anything about history, you know it's all in vain.<br/><br/>Honestly, the story is pretty meh, and I'd have given it 2-stars because it's bearable and at least this one tries to tie everything together. Only problem is the parts that don't relate to the story. Specifically, Magnus's thoughts about the French Revolution, which are ambivalent. Why, yo</span>
  <span id="freeText5033117671413652443" style="display:none">Full review <a href="http://snarktheater.tumblr.com/post/133949388634/the-bane-chronicles-the-runaway-queen" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog, the Snark Theater</a>.<br /><br />In this story, Magnus helps Queen Marie Antoinette escape the Tuileries, as well as a bunch of vampires. If you know anything about history, you know it's all in vain.<br /><br />Honestly, the story is pretty meh, and I'd have given it 2-stars because it's bearable and at least this one tries to tie everything together. Only problem is the parts that don't relate to the story. Specifically, Magnus's thoughts about the French Revolution, which are ambivalent. Why, you ask? Because on one hand, he "feels" for the poor who can barely eat, and on the other, the nobles had extravagant fashion. I shit you not.<br /><br />And it when it comes time for him to choose a side (i.e. decide to help Marie Antoinette or not), what sways him over is a pretty boy. Because of course it's a pretty boy. Is there <i>anything</i> in Clare books that don't have everything to do with pretty boys? If Alec had sided with Valentine, I'm pretty sure Magnus would have happily let him wreck the world in <i>The Mortal Instruments</i>.<br /><br /><br />Also, it's only the second story, but so far, the only people Magnus has been involved with that have been developed and shown to us as relevant are men. He's also been given three female lovers so far, but two were offhanded mention and one was barely developed (and their romance was literally skipped over). If you want to write a bi character, <i>write a bi character</i>, but beyond that, it really feels like the authors don't <i>want</i> to write about a female love interest. As I said, everything in Clare books relies on pretty boys. And it's striking me as a little bit sexist.<br /><br />We'll see if it continues throughout the series or if I'm reaching too far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5033117671413652443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_622331748" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622331748" />
    <a title="Julieta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15807512-julieta"><img alt="Julieta" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622331748?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julieta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julieta" href="/user/show/15807512-julieta">Julieta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15807512-julieta?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15807512-julieta?shelf=extras">extras</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622331748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer117641811333719418">This was a nice surprise. After reading What really happened in Peru and being completely disappointed I was expecting the worst from this story but I enjoyed it. The first part is a little boring and kind of pointless, especially the first paragraph, I was really tempted to not continue after it, but it gets better later. <br/>What bothered me a little was the use of french terms and french words without explanation. I always enjoy Cassie's use of different languages in her books but there is always</span>
  <span id="freeText117641811333719418" style="display:none">This was a nice surprise. After reading What really happened in Peru and being completely disappointed I was expecting the worst from this story but I enjoyed it. The first part is a little boring and kind of pointless, especially the first paragraph, I was really tempted to not continue after it, but it gets better later. <br />What bothered me a little was the use of french terms and french words without explanation. I always enjoy Cassie's use of different languages in her books but there is always some other character who doesn't understand it and we get some kind of explanation. <br />Also, some parts have lot of word repetition which drives me insane.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I found a little bit too crazy how Magnus called and glamoured the hot air balloon to escape (like it wasn't impossible enough that they escape using a hot air balloon that Magnus has no idea how to make it work). It was too much. It's like there are no limits for Magnus' magic which I don't think it's true, even if he is The High Warlock of Brooklyn.<br />And the fact that Axel ends up kissing Magnus bothered me, he is obviously in love with Marie Antoinette and I didn't think he would be attracted by Magnus at any point. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This story renews my hope on the Chronicles, I will be waiting foward to the next one :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="117641811333719418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i2Q+paSbsHn68w8L+G+w8CUHJCjg/gMCyTOeiICGdjpQ9GXyzreK1n75P+9QAMjtQPBKzDdvT16x42NzfNnxmQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CuJbq8iPTb5d7JJbHC065I+KD2j+ApSlZ+CYJJ6v2KDRcgD8oqN3Ednmor+0QkL56n1hjCmT2PkfMGXfYvBfAw==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_45141804').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_45141804').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer9214346410488765285">Hello Goodreadsers.   <span id="freeText9214346410488765285" style="display:none">Hello Goodreadsers. Here's my official bio:<br /><br />"Cassandra Clare was born overseas and spent her early years traveling around the world with her family and several trunks of fantasy books. Cassandra worked for several years as an entertainment journalist for the Hollywood Reporter before turning her attention to fiction. She is the author of City of Bones, the first book in the Mortal Instruments trilogy and a New York Times bestseller. Cassandra lives with her fiance and their two cats in Massachusetts."<br /><br />You can find me online at <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.cassandraclare.com">www.cassandraclare.com</a><br /><br />I have a blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/">http://cassandraclare.livejournal.com/</a><br /><br />and a Facebook:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare">http://www.facebook.com/Cassandraclare</a><br /><br />and a Twitter:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.twitter.com/cassieclare">www.twitter.com/cassieclare</a><br /><br />I'll be available here on Goodreads to answer questions for a Goodreads Author Discussion starting September 18 — <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/37113.Q_A_with_Cassandra_Clare">http://www.goodreads.com/group/show/3...</a><br /><br />Go sign up so you don't miss the conversation when it starts!</span>
